</p><p>In 2011, Page bought the $45-million 193-foot (59&#160;m) <a href="/wiki/Superyacht" title="Superyacht">superyacht</a> <i>Senses</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Later on, Page announced on his <a href="/wiki/Google%2B" title="Google+">Google+</a> profile in May 2013 that his right <a href="/wiki/Vocal_cord" class="mw-redirect" title="Vocal cord">vocal cord</a> is paralyzed from a cold that he contracted the previous summer, while his left cord was paralyzed in 1999, and that the doctors were unable to identify the exact cause.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Google+ post also revealed that Page had made a large donation to a vocal-cord nerve-function research program at the Voice Health Institute in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>. An anonymous source stated that the donation exceeded $20 million.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In October 2013, <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">Business Insider</a></i> reported that Page's paralysis were caused by an <a href="/wiki/Autoimmune_disease" title="Autoimmune disease">autoimmune disease</a> called <a href="/wiki/Hashimoto%27s_thyroiditis" title="Hashimoto&#39;s thyroiditis">Hashimoto's thyroiditis</a>, and prevented him from undertaking Google quarterly earnings conference calls for an indefinite period.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2014, Page's family foundation, the Carl Victor Page Memorial Fund, reportedly holding assets in excess of a billion dollars at the end of 2013, gave $15 million to aid the effort against the <a href="/wiki/Ebola_virus_epidemic_in_West_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa">Ebola virus epidemic in West Africa</a>. Page wrote on his Google+ page that "My wife and I just donated $15 million [...] Our hearts go out to everyone affected."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2021 it was revealed that Page holds a <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> resident's visa and had traveled to the country on a <a href="/wiki/Medical_evacuation" title="Medical evacuation">medivac</a> flight from <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a> for his son's treatment in New Zealand. The flight took place on January 12, 2021. Page had been living in Fiji with his family during the duration of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2023, the <a href="/wiki/Us_virgin_islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Us virgin islands">US Virgin Islands</a> tried several times to serve Page a subpoena in the lawsuit over <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase</a>'s links to <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Epstein" title="Jeffrey Epstein">Jeffrey Epstein</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Page has purchased multiple private islands across the Caribbean and South Pacific, including the <a href="/wiki/Hans_Lollik_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Hans Lollik Island">Hans Lollik Island</a> in 2014, <a href="/wiki/Eustatia_Island" title="Eustatia Island">Eustatia Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cayo_Norte" title="Cayo Norte">Cayo Norte</a> in 2018, and <a href="/wiki/Tavarua" title="Tavarua">Tavarua</a> in 2020.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2025, Page and Brin, worth a combined $520 billion, terminated or moved out of California sixty limited liability companies that hold their assets.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-NYT&#95;2026-01-09&#95;130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_2026-01-09-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Awards_and_accolades">Awards and accolades</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="1998–2009"><span id="1998.E2.80.932009"></span>1998–2009</h3></div>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/PC_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="PC Magazine">PC Magazine</a></i> has praised Google as among the Top 100 Web Sites and Search Engines (1998) and awarded Google the Technical Excellence Award for Innovation in Web Application Development in 1999. In 2000, Google earned a <a href="/wiki/Webby_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Webby Award">Webby Award</a>, a People's Voice Award for technical achievement, and in 2001, was awarded Outstanding Search Service, Best Image Search Engine, Best Design, Most Webmaster Friendly Search Engine, and Best Search Feature at the Search Engine Watch Awards.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2002, Page was named a <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> Global Leader for Tomorrow<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and along with Brin, was named by the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a> (MIT)'s <i><a href="/wiki/Technology_Review" class="mw-redirect" title="Technology Review">Technology Review</a></i> publication as one of the top 100 innovators in the world under the age of 35, as part of its yearly <a href="/wiki/TR35" class="mw-redirect" title="TR35">TR100</a> listing (changed to "TR35" after 2005).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2003, both Page and Brin received an MBA from <a href="/wiki/IE_Business_School" title="IE Business School">IE Business School</a>, in an <a href="/wiki/Honorary_degree" title="Honorary degree">honorary</a> capacity, "for embodying the entrepreneurial spirit and lending momentum to the creation of new businesses."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2004, they received the <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Marconi Foundation">Marconi Foundation</a>'s prize and were elected <a href="/wiki/Fellow" title="Fellow">Fellows</a> of the Marconi Foundation at <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University" title="Columbia University">Columbia University</a>. In announcing their selection, John Jay Iselin, the Foundation's president, congratulated the two men for "their invention that has fundamentally changed the way information is retrieved today."<sup id="cite&#95;ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2004, Page and Brin received the Golden Plate Award of the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Achievement" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy of Achievement">American Academy of Achievement</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Page and Brin were also Award Recipients and National Finalists for the EY Entrepreneur of the Year Award in 2003.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Also in 2004, X PRIZE chose Page as a trustee of their board<sup id="cite&#95;ref-corpexecs&#95;138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-corpexecs-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and he was elected to the National Academy of Engineering.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-:0&#95;132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2005, Brin and Page were elected Fellows of the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2008 Page received the <a href="/wiki/Princess_of_Asturias_Awards#Communications_and_Humanities_(Comunicación_y_Humanidades)" title="Princess of Asturias Awards">Communication Award</a> from <a href="/wiki/Felipe_VI_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Felipe VI of Spain">Prince Felipe</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince of Asturias Awards">Prince of Asturias Awards</a> on behalf of Google.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Since_2009">Since 2009</h3></div>
<ul><li>In 2009, Page received an honorary doctorate from the University of Michigan during a graduation commencement ceremony.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2011, he was ranked 24th on the <a href="/wiki/Forbes_list_of_billionaires" class="mw-redirect" title="Forbes list of billionaires">Forbes list of billionaires</a>, and as the 11th richest person in the U.S.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-forbes&#95;2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In 2015, Page's "Powerful People" profile on the <i>Forbes</i> site states that Google is "the most influential company of the digital era".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>As of July 2014, the Bloomberg Billionaires Index lists Page as the 17th richest man in the world, with an estimated net worth of $32.7 billion.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>At the completion of 2014, <i>Fortune</i> magazine named Page its "Businessperson of the Year", declaring him "the world's most daring CEO".<sup id="cite&#95;ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In October 2015, Page was named number one on the <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> "America's Most Popular Chief Executives" list, as voted by Google's employees.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In August 2017, Page was awarded honorary citizenship of <a href="/wiki/Agrigento" title="Agrigento">Agrigento</a>, Italy.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</h2></div>
<p>A fictionalized version of Larry Page portrayed by actor <a href="/wiki/Ben_Feldman" title="Ben Feldman">Ben Feldman</a> appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Showtime_(TV_network)" title="Showtime (TV network)">Showtime</a> drama series <a href="/wiki/Super_Pumped_(TV_series)" title="Super Pumped (TV series)"><i>Super Pumped</i></a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

A trust with ties to Mr. Page also purchased a $71.9 million mansion in Miami's Coconut Grove neighborhood this week, according to a deed seen by The Times. Another entity jointly managed by Mr. Brin and Mr. Page moved out of California and to Nevada on Christmas Eve, according to a filing seen by The Times. The Google founders' shrinking connections to California underscore the impact of a potential ballot measure that would affect the state's wealthiest residents.</q></cite><span title="ctx&#95;ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft&#95;val&#95;fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=New+York+Times&amp;rft.atitle=Google+Guys+Say+Bye+to+California&amp;rft.date=2026-01-09&amp;rft.aulast=Mac&amp;rft.aufirst=Ryan&amp;rft.au=Schleifer%2C+Theodore&amp;rft.au=Knight%2C+Heather&amp;rft&#95;id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nytimes.com%2F2026%2F01%2F09%2Ftechnology%2Fgoogle-founders-california-wealth-tax.html&amp;rfr&#95;id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALarry+Page" class="Z3988"></span> </span>
